###begin p 32
###xml 68 71 68 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 76 79 76 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 93 94 93 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 100 101 100 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 131 134 131 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 139 142 139 142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 268 271 268 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aci</italic>
###xml 316 318 316 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 355 358 355 358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aci</italic>
###xml 384 389 384 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 495 500 495 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 596 599 596 599 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 601 610 601 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g002">Figure 2C</xref>
###xml 652 657 652 657 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 703 708 703 708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 751 754 751 754 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 756 765 756 765 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
###xml 831 834 831 834 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aci</italic>
###xml 870 873 870 873 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 957 962 957 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 992 995 992 995 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aci</italic>
###xml 1021 1024 1021 1024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1097 1102 1097 1102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 1107 1112 1107 1112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 1114 1123 1114 1123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
###xml 1248 1253 1248 1253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 1258 1263 1258 1263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 1422 1427 1422 1427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 1576 1579 1576 1579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1584 1587 1584 1587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
These results point to the possibility that the interaction between HML and HMR involves the E- and I-silencer elements that flank HML and HMR on their 5' and 3' side, respectively. To test this we repeated the 3C analysis with a frequently cutting restriction enzyme AciI that cuts at multiple locations within the HM loci. We find that the small 814 bp AciI fragment containing the HMR-I element (genomic position 294510-295324) most strongly interacts with the 821 bp fragment containing the HML-E silencer (genomic position 10815-11636), and significantly less frequently with other parts of HML (Figure 2C). Conversely the fragment containing the HML-E silencer interacts most prominently with the HMR-I fragment, as compared to other regions of HMR (Figure 2D). As a control we determined crosslinking frequencies between an AciI fragment located in the middle of HML. This fragment (genomic position 11679-11906) interacted most prominently with the HMR-I fragment and the neighboring AciI fragment located within HMR, but the crosslinking frequencies were lower than that observed between HML-E and HMR-I (Figure 2D), which is as expected for a fragment located just next to the site of interaction. These results strongly suggest that the HML-E and HMR-I silencers, or elements located very close to them, are the sites of interaction. Despite intense efforts, we have not been able to generate a mutant in which HMR-I was deleted without also creating unexplained rearrangements in the locus. Therefore we cannot unequivocally conclude that the interactions between HML and HMR are directly mediated by the silencer elements.
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 58 59 58 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 65 66 65 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 119 120 119 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 126 127 126 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 172 188 172 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g002">Figure 2E and 2F</xref>
###xml 213 216 213 216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aci</italic>
###xml 244 247 244 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Aci</italic>
###xml 270 275 270 275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 280 285 280 285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 349 354 349 354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 359 364 359 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 456 459 456 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 464 467 464 467 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 670 674 670 674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gheldof1">[33]</xref>
###xml 675 679 675 679 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dekker2">[34]</xref>
###xml 680 684 680 684 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dekker3">[36]</xref>
###xml 701 706 701 706 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 711 716 711 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 760 763 760 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 768 771 768 771 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 863 866 863 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 866 867 866 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 866 867 866 867 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 872 875 872 875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 914 919 910 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 924 929 920 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 935 940 931 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-I</italic>
###xml 945 950 941 946 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 1047 1058 1043 1054 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g002">Figure 2E,F</xref>
###xml 1392 1393 1388 1389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 1399 1400 1395 1396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">I</italic>
###xml 1420 1422 1416 1418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1489 1491 1485 1487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Given the interaction observed between regions containing E- and I-silencers from opposite loci, we then asked whether E- and I-silencers from the same loci also interact (Figure 2E and 2F). 3C analysis using the AciI enzyme indicates that the AciI fragments containing HML-E and HMR-E elements interact frequently with nearby sites. Interestingly, HML-E and HMR-E interacted more strongly with sites within the silent loci than with sites located outside HML and HMR, despite being separated by comparable genomic distances. One explanation could be that the silent loci are more compact than active chromatin, which can result in increased 3C crosslinking frequencies [33],[34],[36]. Alternatively, HML-E and HMR-E interact preferentially with a site within HML and HMR respectively. Interestingly, we note that the peak of interaction is near the promoters of HMRa and HMLalpha Importantly, the interactions of HML-E and HMR-E with HML-I and HMR-I respectively were significantly less frequent than other interactions throughout these regions (Figure 2E,F). If a loop existed between silencer elements within a given locus these preferred interactions would stand out as peaks on top of a less frequent background of interactions. Our results indicate that although cross-linking frequencies are generally increased within the silent loci, there is no preferential interaction between the E- and I- silencers of each HM locus as compared to interactions with other sites throughout the HM loci.
###end p 33
###begin title 34
###xml 30 33 30 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 38 41 38 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
Sir Proteins Are Required for HML and HMR Interaction
###end title 34
###begin p 35
###xml 21 24 21 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 29 32 29 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 172 181 172 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
###xml 183 192 179 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 197 206 189 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2&#916;</italic>
###xml 257 260 245 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 265 268 253 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 288 292 276 280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Aparicio1">[41]</xref>
###xml 317 320 305 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 325 328 313 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 351 355 339 343 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4</italic>
###xml 362 366 346 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3</italic>
###xml 376 380 356 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2</italic>
###xml 402 411 378 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
###xml 435 438 411 414 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 548 551 524 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 635 639 611 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR2</italic>
###xml 644 648 620 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR3</italic>
To determine whether HML and HMR need to be in a heterochromatic state for them to interact, we analyzed mutants that are defective in silencing. We first chose to analyze sir4Delta, sir3Delta and sir2Delta cells, because in these mutants silencing at both HML and HMR is completely lost [41]. Using 3C, we find that HMR and HML no longer interact in sir4Delta, sir3Delta and sir2Delta mutant strains (Figure 3A). Interactions between HMR and the adjacent right telomere are not affected to a similar extent. Interestingly, the interaction between HMR and the right telomere is reduced in the absence of Sir4p but not upon deletion of SIR2 and SIR3. This observation could be related to the degree of peripheral anchoring of these loci (see below).
###end p 35
###begin title 36
###xml 30 32 30 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Role of silencing proteins in HM interactions.
###end title 36
###begin p 37
###xml 32 41 32 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
###xml 43 52 39 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 54 63 46 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2&#916;</italic>
###xml 65 74 53 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 76 85 60 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc2&#916;</italic>
###xml 90 98 70 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2-345</italic>
###xml 152 155 132 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 178 181 158 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 280 287 260 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 306 315 286 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
###xml 317 326 293 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 328 337 300 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2&#916;</italic>
###xml 342 351 310 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 392 400 356 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g001">Figure 1</xref>
(A) Analysis of interactions in sir4Delta, sir3Delta, sir2Delta, sir1Delta, esc2Delta and sir2-345 cells examining crosslinking frequencies between the EcoRI fragment containing HMR with other restriction fragments along the length of chromosome III. (B) 3D live cell analysis of HML-HMR colocalization in sir4Delta, sir3Delta, sir2Delta and sir1Delta cells. Image stacks were acquired as in Figure 1 and analyzed by the SpotDistance plug-in of ImageJ. R software was used for the representation of distance distributions as a box plot. Outliers are defined as 1.5 times the Inter Quartile Range (IQR) and are represented as open circles. Distance frequencies were compared using a Wilcox test.
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 49 52 49 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 57 60 57 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 136 140 136 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4</italic>
###xml 150 159 146 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 237 246 229 238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 313 316 293 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 321 324 301 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 377 386 357 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
###xml 467 476 443 452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 493 502 469 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 535 538 507 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 543 546 515 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 607 616 579 588 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 664 668 636 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3</italic>
###xml 688 692 656 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4</italic>
###xml 944 947 908 911 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 948 951 912 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
In agreement with the 3C data, colocalization of HML and HMR, as determined by live cell fluorescence microscopy, is largely reduced in sir4Delta and sir3Delta cells, in which only 5% and 7% of distances scored are <250 nm respectively (Figure 3B). As compared to wild-type where in approximately60% of the cells HML and HMR are found colocalized or adjacent to each other, in sir4Delta cells the distance between these loci is less than 500 nm in only 21% of cells (Figure 3B). Similarly, in sir3Delta cells <35% of cells scored show HML and HMR colocalized or immediately adjacent to each other (n = 500; Figure 3B). The distribution of 3D distances measured in sir3Delta (n = 500) and sir4Delta (n = 307) cells is clearly shifted to greater distances as compared to wt (n = 836). These results indicate that the heterochromatic structure established by the Sir complex or the Sir4p, Sir3p, and Sir2p proteins themselves are critical for the HML-HMR interaction.
###end p 38
###begin p 39
###xml 102 105 102 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 110 113 110 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 195 199 195 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Pillus1">[42]</xref>
###xml 216 218 216 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 278 282 278 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4</italic>
###xml 289 293 285 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3</italic>
###xml 304 308 296 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2</italic>
###xml 326 335 314 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 342 345 326 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 350 353 334 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 410 421 394 405 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3A,B</xref>
###xml 502 504 486 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 593 609 577 593 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s002">Figure S2G and H</xref>
To extend our study, we asked whether Sir1p, a protein that interacts with silencer elements flanking HML and HMR via the Rap1p/ORC complex during the establishment of the silent chromatin state [42] participates in HM loci interactions. Interestingly, we find that, similar to sir4Delta, sir3Delta, and sir2Delta mutants, in sir1Delta cells HMR and HML no longer interact as shown by 3C and by 3D microscopy (Figure 3A,B), despite significant residual silencing (see below). Interactions between each HM locus and the telomere on the opposite end of chromosome III are concomitantly reduced (Figure S2G and H).
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 32 41 32 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 169 173 165 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dhillon1">[43]</xref>
###xml 243 245 239 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 325 327 321 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 397 400 393 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 422 426 418 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Cuperus1">[44]</xref>
###xml 480 484 476 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Cuperus1">[44]</xref>
###xml 588 590 584 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 596 600 592 596 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dhillon1">[43]</xref>
###xml 614 618 610 614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ESC2</italic>
###xml 658 662 654 658 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dhillon1">[43]</xref>
###xml 701 710 697 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 743 747 735 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ESC2</italic>
###xml 802 805 794 797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 810 813 802 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 815 824 807 816 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
###xml 875 882 867 874 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 934 936 926 928 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Given the results obtained with sir1Delta cells we chose to determine the role of Esc2p that has been identified as a protein that can functionally substitute for Sir1p [43]. Although it is currently not known whether Esc2p directly binds the HM loci, there is strong evidence suggesting that Esc2p is directly affecting the HM loci. First, Esc2p was identified as a protein that when targeted to HML can induce silencing [44]. Second, Esc2p has been shown to directly bind Sir2p [44]. Third, overproduction of Esc2p can substitute for Sir1p and aids in the establishment of silencing at HM loci [43]. Deletion of ESC2 has only minimal effects on silencing ([43], and see below). Interestingly, as in sir1Delta cells, we find that deletion of ESC2 completely abolished the specific interaction between HML and HMR (Figure 3A). We conclude that Esc2p plays a critical role in HML-HMR interactions, presumably by directly acting on the HM loci, although we cannot formally rule out a more indirect role.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 82 85 82 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 90 93 90 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 325 329 325 329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Yang1">[45]</xref>
###xml 342 350 342 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2-345</italic>
###xml 516 520 516 520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Imai1">[23]</xref>
###xml 527 535 527 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2-345</italic>
###xml 567 570 567 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 575 578 575 578 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 612 621 612 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3A</xref>
###xml 810 812 810 812 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Furthermore, given the importance of the silencers and silencing proteins for the HML and HMR interaction, we chose to analyze a mutant in which silencing proteins are recruited (albeit to a lesser extent than in wild-type) and assembled at the silencers but in which the Sir complex fails to spread across the silenced loci [45]. The mutant sir2-345 contains a point mutation at residue 345, which results in an Asn-to-Ala substitution. This mutant lacks deacetylase activity which results in a defect in silencing [23]. In a sir2-345 mutant, an interaction between HML and HMR can no longer be detected by 3C (Figure 3A). This indicates that in order for this interaction to occur proper heterochromatin must be formed and that the mere presence of Sir proteins at the silencers is not sufficient to promote HM loci interaction.
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 50 51 50 51 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</bold>
###xml 81 84 77 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 89 92 85 88 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 239 246 235 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 273 276 269 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir</italic>
###xml 391 394 387 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 399 402 395 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 445 455 441 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s003">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 487 490 483 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 491 494 487 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 511 520 507 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
###xml 522 531 514 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 533 542 521 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2&#916;</italic>
###xml 548 557 532 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
A defect in silencing leads to expression of both a- and alpha- information from HMR and HML respectively, as in diploid cells (i.e. they display defects in mating). Therefore, we analyzed a diploid strain to determine whether the loss of HML-HMR interaction is due to the sir mutant cell's diploid characteristics. We found no significant difference in the crosslinking frequencies between HML and HMR in wild type diploid and haploid strains (Figure S3A). We conclude that the loss of HML-HMR interactions in sir4Delta, sir3Delta, sir2Delta, and sir1Delta mutants is not due to the cell's diploid-like state.
###end p 42
###begin title 43
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 4 7 4 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
HML-HMR Interaction Does Not Require Nuclear Periphery Attachment
###end title 43
###begin p 44
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 8 11 8 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 103 107 103 107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Palladino1">[12]</xref>
###xml 108 112 108 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gotta1">[13]</xref>
###xml 295 298 295 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 303 306 303 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 621 623 621 623 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 694 698 694 698 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gartenberg1">[46]</xref>
###xml 699 703 699 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 909 913 909 913 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Hediger1">[16]</xref>
###xml 915 919 915 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 920 924 920 924 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Laroche1">[49]</xref>
###xml 935 937 935 937 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 971 975 971 975 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
HML and HMR, as well as the telomeres, are clustered in silent compartments near the nuclear periphery [12],[13]. We questioned whether anchoring of these loci to the nuclear envelope (NE) may facilitate long-range interactions between them. To address this issue we wished to determine whether HML and HMR can interact and colocalize when their peripheral localization was disrupted. Two partially redundant pathways are involved in tethering heterochromatic loci such as telomeres to the NE. The first pathway is dependent on the Sir4p and Esc1p proteins. It has previously been shown in G1 cells that anchoring of the HM loci to the NE is reduced in cells deleted for Sir complex components [46],[47] and that Sir-dependent anchoring requires Esc1p. The second pathway requires the yKu70p/yKu80p heterodimer. If either one of these genes is deleted most telomeres are partially released from the periphery [16], [47]-[49], although HM loci remain peripherally located [47].
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 0 8 0 8 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 42 44 42 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 245 248 245 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tet</italic>
###xml 248 250 248 250 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">op</sup>
###xml 255 258 255 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lac</italic>
###xml 258 260 258 260 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">op</sup>
###xml 275 278 275 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 283 286 283 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 381 385 381 385 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 386 390 386 390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Hediger2">[50]</xref>
###xml 743 747 743 747 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4</italic>
###xml 761 765 757 761 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 767 775 763 771 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 834 843 830 835 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
###xml 854 858 846 850 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3</italic>
###xml 902 905 890 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 910 913 898 901 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 994 1002 982 990 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1014 1023 1002 1007 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 1108 1111 1092 1095 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1116 1119 1100 1103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1121 1129 1105 1113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1239 1248 1223 1228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1260 1262 1240 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Figure 4 shows the radial position of the HM loci for WT and mutant strains in interphase (and not only G1) cells to be directly comparable with 3C studies that involve analysis of non-synchronized cultures (see below). Nuclear positions of the tetop and lacop tagged silent HML and HMR loci were visualized using TetR or LacI repressor-GFP fusion proteins in G1 and S-phase cells [47],[50]. Data were acquired in three dimensions to assign the position of the resulting fluorescent spot relative to the GFP-tagged NE (Nup49-GFP) in the focal plane in which it was brightest and in one of three concentric nuclear zones of equal surface. Enrichment of the silent mating type loci near the nuclear envelope in wild-type cells is abolished in a sir4Delta strain [[47]; Figure 4]. Interestingly, we find that this effect is specific for sir4Delta cells: in sir3Delta mutants significant anchoring of both HML and HMR was retained, possibly due to binding of Sir4p to the silencer nucleation site (Figure 4). Since in sir3Delta mutant strains we no longer detected preferential interaction and colocalization of HML and HMR (Figure 3), we conclude that proximity to the NE is not sufficient for their interaction. In addition, we find that in esc1Delta cells, the HM loci maintain their peripheral localization. This suggests that Sir4p containing heterochromatin can associate with the nuclear periphery in an Esc1p-independent manner.
###end p 45
###begin title 46
###xml 33 36 33 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 41 44 41 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
Preferred peripheral position of HML and HMR.
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 80 83 80 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 88 91 88 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 104 113 104 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 115 124 111 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
###xml 127 136 119 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 141 150 129 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 166 169 150 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 169 170 153 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 393 394 377 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
Positions were mapped relative to the nuclear envelope in strains of GFP-tagged HML and HMR loci in WT, sir3Delta, sir4Delta, yku70Delta and esc1Delta G1 and S phase MATa cells. Data are represented in bar graphs as the percentage of spots in 3 concentric zones of equal surface. The number of cells analyzed (n) is indicated. * indicates a distribution identical to random (33% in each zone; P>0.05) in a  analysis. Bar is 1 microm.
###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 8 11 8 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 145 148 145 148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 195 198 195 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 249 253 249 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 255 263 255 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 333 336 333 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 346 356 346 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 399 402 395 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 409 413 405 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 438 441 434 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 600 602 596 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 652 654 648 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 752 754 748 750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
HML and HMR are also both directly associated with the nuclear periphery in a manner that does not require yKu70p. In interphase the position of HMR is unaffected by the absence of yKu70p, while HML's anchoring to the NE is significantly increased ([47], Figure 4). Further, the increase in peripheral localization of the GFP-tagged HML locus in yku70Delta cells is dependent on the presence of the HML locus [47]. Similarly, deletion of HMR reduces the peripheral localization of the right end of chromosome III (KB, unpublished observations). These analyses suggest that peripheral localization of HM loci is not solely due to the close proximity of HM loci to telomeres that are often anchored to the nuclear periphery and further indicate that the HM loci strongly contribute to the peripheral localization of the ends of chromosome III.
###end p 48
###begin p 49
###xml 42 46 42 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ESC1</italic>
###xml 51 56 51 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YKU70</italic>
###xml 142 145 142 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 150 153 150 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 223 231 223 231 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 361 364 361 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 483 488 483 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YKU70</italic>
###xml 493 497 493 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ESC1</italic>
###xml 565 568 565 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 575 579 575 579 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gartenberg1">[46]</xref>
###xml 739 741 739 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Next we analyzed strains deleted for both ESC1 and YKU70 in which both anchoring pathways are abolished. We find that peripheral anchoring of HML and HMR was only slightly but not significantly reduced in interphase cells (Figure 4). Anchoring was somewhat more reduced in G1 than in S phase cells (data not shown). These observations on the radial position of HMR in its native chromosomal location extend those reported by Gartenberg and colleagues who found that deletion of both YKU70 and ESC1 resulted in loss of peripheral localization of an extrachromosomal HMR locus [46]. Our results suggest that chromosomal context plays a role in peripheral localization. We conclude that alternative Sir4p-dependent pathways exist that anchor HM loci to the nuclear periphery.
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 17 19 17 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 43 53 43 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 61 70 57 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 141 144 133 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 149 152 141 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 194 203 186 195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 219 223 211 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">KU80</italic>
###xml 285 304 277 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ku70&#916; esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 324 327 308 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 328 331 312 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 473 476 457 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 481 484 465 468 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
Next we analyzed HM interactions by 3C. In yku70Delta and in esc1Delta cells, we observed a significant increase in the frequency with which HML and HMR interact as compared to wild type cells (Figure 5A). Deletion of YKU80 did not significantly affect the crosslinking frequency. In yku70Delta esc1Delta double mutants the HML-HMR crosslinking frequency is slightly higher than in either single mutant. These results demonstrate that yKu70p and Esc1p are not required for HML and HMR to specifically interact.
###end p 50
###begin title 51
###xml 0 2 0 2 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
HM Interaction is independent of telomere anchorage mutants.
###end title 51
###begin p 52
###xml 35 45 35 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 47 57 43 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku80&#916;</italic>
###xml 59 68 51 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 70 93 58 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">and yku70&#916;esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 148 153 128 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EcoRI</italic>
###xml 174 177 154 157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 276 283 256 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 302 312 282 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 314 323 290 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 329 347 301 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ku70&#916;esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 401 409 365 373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 437 440 401 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>

###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 17 20 17 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 21 24 21 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 95 104 95 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g005">Figure 5B</xref>
###xml 110 119 110 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 156 159 152 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 164 167 160 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 271 272 267 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 287 291 283 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1</italic>
###xml 297 302 293 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70</italic>
###xml 314 317 306 309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 322 325 314 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 533 536 525 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 541 544 533 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 671 672 663 664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 679 681 671 673 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;6</sup>
###xml 688 698 680 686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 753 763 741 747 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 893 897 877 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Maillet2">[51]</xref>
###xml 940 943 924 927 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 948 951 932 935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 955 974 939 950 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1061 1064 1037 1040 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1069 1072 1045 1048 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1134 1143 1110 1119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g005">Figure 5B</xref>
We also analyzed HML-HMR colocalization in these strains by live cell fluorescence microscopy (Figure 5B). In esc1Delta cells 51% of cells measured exhibit HML and HMR colocalization or juxtaposition (n = 391), which is comparable to what we observed in wild type cells (P = 0.063 wt vs esc1). In yku70Delta cells HML and HMR are found colocalized in 18% of the cells and adjacent to each other in another 28% of cells (n = 814). The frequency of co-localization is comparable to wild type, but the distribution of distances between HML and HMR differs from wild type. It appears that in the absence of yKu70p more nuclei display widely separated loci than in wild type (P = 6.1e-6 wt vs yku70Delta). This may be related to the fact that populations of yku70Delta cells display two semi-stable states of silencing: one in which telomeres are delocalized and one in which they remain clustered [51]. Finally, we found that colocalization of HML and HMR in yku70Deltaesc1Delta double mutants was also comparable to wild type: 52% of the cells measured still show HML and HMR colocalized or immediately adjacent to each other (n = 165) (Figure 5B).
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 72 75 60 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 76 79 64 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 302 304 290 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 372 374 360 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
We note that the 3C analysis revealed a approximately4-fold increase in HML-HMR interactions in all three mutants, but that live cell fluorescence failed to detect an increase in colocalization of these loci. The increased crosslinking frequency as detected by 3C may be due to loss of interactions of HM loci with telomeres, which could result in an increased chance for HM loci to become ligated in the 3C assay or due to a more intimate association that is more easily crosslinked (see discussion).
###end p 54
###begin p 55
###xml 25 28 25 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 29 32 29 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 403 406 403 406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 407 410 407 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 502 505 502 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 510 513 510 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 591 598 591 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 685 693 685 693 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 696 705 696 705 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 863 866 863 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 871 874 871 874 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1212 1215 1212 1215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1220 1223 1220 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1334 1337 1334 1337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1342 1345 1342 1345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1557 1566 1557 1566 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 1600 1603 1600 1603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1608 1611 1608 1611 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1651 1654 1651 1654 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1658 1661 1658 1661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1773 1776 1773 1776 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1803 1806 1803 1806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1953 1956 1953 1956 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1960 1963 1960 1963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 2155 2158 2155 2158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 2163 2166 2163 2166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
These analyses show that HML-HMR interactions do not require the known membrane anchors yKu70p/yKu80p and Esc1p. However, their peripheral localization was also not abolished in the absence of both these membrane anchors. Our inability to genetically disrupt peripheral localization of the silent mating type loci prevented us from directly assessing the influence of membrane anchoring on facilitating HML-HMR interactions. Therefore, as an alternative approach, we set out to follow the positions of HML and HMR in wild type living cells over several minutes in order to determine whether HML-HMR interactions can be observed in the interior of the nucleus or only at the periphery (Figure 6). Figure 6A shows a representative movie comprising a series of 50 2D images taken at 10 s intervals of interphase cells on a wide-field Olympus XI inverted microscope. HML and HMR tags colocalized either near the NE as identified by the nuclear pore component Nup49p fused to CFP, or at the center of the nuclei imaged. In addition, colocalization was a transient event, because, after a few minutes, separation of previously colocalized loci was observed (compare time points 9 and 12 or time points 4 and 5). Thus, HML and HMR seem to collide and separate both at peripheral and internal nuclear locations. In order to determine whether HML and HMR were more likely to interact at the nuclear periphery, we followed their position relative to the nuclear center in single nuclei over time taking images in 2D every 1.5 seconds on a confocal LSM510 microscope. Figure 6B summarizes the distances between HML and HMR plotted against the distance of either HML or HMR to the nuclear center at every time point during nine 1-2 min time lapse movies (n = 676). We found that in 2D HML is separated <250 nm from HMR (colocalization) in >45% of the time points scored. Moreover, the probability of colocalization was similar in the interior fraction (position of HML or HMR less than 720 nm from the nuclear center, about 2/3 of the positions) and the peripheral fraction of the nucleus. These movies clearly demonstrate that over long periods, interaction between HML and HMR was independent of NE anchoring.
###end p 55
###begin title 56
###xml 20 23 20 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 28 31 28 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
Interaction between HML and HMR is independent of peripheral anchoring.
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 44 47 44 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 52 55 52 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 311 314 311 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 319 322 319 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 450 453 446 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 458 461 454 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 671 674 667 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 679 682 675 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 887 890 883 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 894 897 890 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
(A) Time lapse images of YFP and CFP tagged HML and HMR relative to the nuclear rim as identified by Nup49-CFP. Images were acquired on a wide-field Olympus XI microscope using a 100x objective (NA = 1.4) every 10 s for 320 s without changing the focal plane. Acquisition times were 400 ms for each wavelength. HML and HMR colocalize transiently near the periphery or in the center of selected nuclei (yellow spots). Bar is 1 microm. (B) Position of HML and HMR relative to the nuclear center inferred from tetR-YFP nuclear fluorescence in single nuclei over time taking images in 2D every 1.5 seconds on a confocal LSM510 microscope plotted against the distance between HML and HMR at every time point during 1-3 min time lapse movies. Colocalization was assigned for distances <250 nm, juxtaposition for distances <500 nm (adjacent). The interior fraction corresponds to a position of HML or HMR at less than 720 nm from the nuclear center, thus about 2/3 of the positions. The percentages represent the fraction of datapoints in any sector of the graph.
###end p 57
###begin title 58
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 8 11 8 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
HML and HMR Interaction Is Dependent on Two Pathways for Nucleosome Assembly
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 198 202 198 202 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Enomoto1">[26]</xref>
###xml 204 208 204 208 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
###xml 210 214 210 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Kaufman1">[52]</xref>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Goodfellow1">[55]</xref>
###xml 303 306 303 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 311 314 311 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 457 461 457 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Kamakaka1">[56]</xref>
###xml 526 530 526 530 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Kaufman2">[57]</xref>
###xml 602 606 602 606 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
###xml 607 611 607 611 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Tyler1">[58]</xref>
###xml 743 746 743 746 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 751 754 751 754 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 754 758 754 758 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
###xml 759 763 759 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Krawitz1">[59]</xref>
###xml 192 197 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 316 321 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Histone chaperones and other proteins involved in nucleosome assembly play roles in gene silencing, heterochromatin formation and heterochromatic clustering in a number of organisms including yeast [26], [27], [52]-[55]. We determined whether these activities are also required for interactions between HML and HMR. Yeast contains two histone assembly complexes. The chromatin assembly factor 1 (CAF-1) complex is involved in nucleosome assembly in S phase [56], whereas the HIR complex functions primarily outside of S phase [57]. The histone chaperone Asf1p stimulates the activity of both complexes [27],[58]. In addition, the HIR and CAF-1 complexes are involved in two parallel, and partially redundant pathways that enhance silencing at HML and HMR[27],[59].
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 81 85 81 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAC1</italic>
###xml 166 169 166 169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 174 177 174 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 201 205 201 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Enomoto1">[26]</xref>
###xml 232 236 232 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAC1</italic>
###xml 277 280 277 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 285 288 285 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 299 308 299 308 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 402 406 402 406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIR1</italic>
###xml 467 470 467 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 475 478 475 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 478 482 478 482 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Kaufman2">[57]</xref>
###xml 491 500 491 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cac1&#916;</italic>
###xml 534 538 530 534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIR1</italic>
###xml 577 580 573 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 581 584 577 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 598 607 594 603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 724 728 720 724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAC1</italic>
###xml 733 737 729 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIR1</italic>
###xml 811 814 807 810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 819 822 815 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 846 855 842 851 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 924 931 920 927 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
First, we tested a strain in which the CAF-1 complex is disrupted by deletion of CAC1. Cac1p is the largest subunit of the CAF-1 complex and in strains lacking Cac1p HML and HMR are weakly derepressed [26]. We find that deletion of CAC1 did not affect the frequency with which HMR and HML interact (Figure 7A). Next we analyzed a strain lacking Hir1p, a subunit of the HIR protein complex. Deletion of HIR1 has also been reported to result in slight de-repression of HML and HMR[57]. As for cac1Delta strains we find that deletion of HIR1 has no effect on the frequency of the HML-HMR interaction (Figure 7A). Given the known functional redundancy of HIR and CAF-1 complexes, we created a double mutant strain in which both CAC1 and HIR1 are deleted. We find that in this case the prominent interaction between HML and HMR is no longer observed (Figure 7A). These results point to a role of nucleosome assembly in mediating HML-HMR interactions, and show that the HIR complex and CAF-1 complex are functionally redundant in this process. Interestingly, in the double mutant, interaction frequencies along the entire chromosome are two- to three-fold higher than the background interactions we observed for all other strains. This may point to a more flexible chromosome organization.
###end p 60
###begin title 61
###xml 39 41 39 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Role of nucleosome assembly factors in HM interactions.
###end title 61
###begin p 62
###xml 32 41 32 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cac1&#916;</italic>
###xml 43 52 39 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 54 72 46 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cac1&#916;hir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 78 87 62 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 141 144 121 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 167 170 147 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 269 276 249 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 295 304 275 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 358 366 334 342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g001">Figure 1</xref>
(A) Analysis of interactions in cac1Delta, hir1Delta, cac1Deltahir1Delta, and asf1Delta cells examining crosslinking frequencies between the EcoRI fragment containing HMR with other restriction fragments along the length of chromosome III. (B) 3D live cell analysis of HML-HMR colocalization in asf1Delta cells. Image stacks were acquired and analyzed as in Figure 1. Distance distributions of various telomere pairs represented in box plots. Probabilities were calculated in R using the Wilcox test.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 246 250 246 250 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Hiraga1">[60]</xref>
###xml 286 295 286 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 327 330 323 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 335 338 331 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 362 371 358 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 396 405 392 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 450 459 442 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g007">Figure 7B</xref>
###xml 526 529 506 509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 534 537 514 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 587 596 567 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 631 634 607 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 639 642 615 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 691 692 667 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 699 702 675 678 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;16</sup>
###xml 713 717 689 693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1</italic>
To further investigate the role of nucleosome assembly, we studied a strain lacking the histone chaperone Asf1p which functions with both the CAF-1 and HIR complex. Recently a role for Asf1p has been proposed for telomere sub-nuclear positioning [60].
