Interestingly, we find that in an asf1Delta mutant the interaction between HML and HMR is no longer observed (Figure 7A). We have also analyzed asf1Delta cells by live cell fluorescence microscopy (Figure 7B). As compared to wild-type where in approximately60% of the cells HML and HMR are found colocalized or adjacent to each other, asf1Delta cells only have 29% of cells with HML and HMR colocalized or adjacent to each other (n = 352; P = 2.2e-16 wt versus asf1).
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 72 76 72 76 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Recht1">[61]</xref>
###xml 77 81 77 81 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Tsubota1">[62]</xref>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Hiraga1">[60]</xref>
###xml 220 224 220 224 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Xu1">[63]</xref>
###xml 360 364 360 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Tsubota1">[62]</xref>
###xml 365 369 365 369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Schneider1">[64]</xref>
###xml 370 374 370 374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Driscoll1">[65]</xref>
###xml 428 431 428 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 436 439 436 439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 540 550 540 550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s003">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 600 609 600 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 179 184 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Asf1p is also required for Histone H3K56 acetylation and its deposition [61],[62]. H3K56 acetylation and deacetylation has been found to play roles in silencing telomeric loci in yeast and tethering of telomere 14L [60],[63]. For this reason we chose to analyze strains which lack Rtt109p, the enzyme that acetylates Histone H3K56 in an Asf1p-dependent manner [62],[64],[65]. We find that in this mutant the interaction between HML and HMR is still observed, albeit with a somewhat reduced crosslinking frequency as compared to wild-type. (Figure S3B). Therefore, the loss of interaction observed in asf1Delta mutants is not solely due to a loss of Histone H3K56 acetylation. Thus, incorrect or unstable tetramer incorporation may lead to poorly organized chromatin that is unfavorable for heterochromatic loci to interact.
###end p 64
###begin title 65
###xml 35 37 35 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Relationship between Silencing and HM Interactions
###end title 65
###begin p 66
###xml 30 33 30 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 34 37 34 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 305 308 305 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 309 312 309 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 327 336 327 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 338 347 334 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc2&#916;</italic>
###xml 349 358 341 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 363 381 351 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cac1&#916;hir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 383 387 363 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
###xml 388 392 368 372 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Pillus1">[42]</xref>
###xml 393 397 373 377 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dhillon1">[43]</xref>
###xml 512 514 492 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 528 532 508 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 536 540 516 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADE2</italic>
###xml 623 625 603 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 983 984 963 964 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 983 984 963 964 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 984 985 964 965 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</italic>
###xml 1010 1013 990 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1018 1026 998 1002 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT&#945;</italic>
###xml 1129 1131 1105 1107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1180 1184 1156 1160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR4</italic>
###xml 1186 1190 1162 1166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR3</italic>
###xml 1192 1196 1168 1172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR2</italic>
###xml 1198 1202 1174 1178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR1</italic>
###xml 1227 1231 1203 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAC1</italic>
###xml 1236 1240 1212 1216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIR1</italic>
###xml 1254 1262 1230 1238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2-345</italic>
###xml 1318 1321 1294 1297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1338 1342 1314 1318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Adh1</italic>
###xml 1390 1398 1366 1374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 1457 1459 1433 1435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1474 1483 1450 1455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc2&#916;</italic>
###xml 1488 1497 1460 1465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1527 1528 1495 1496 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</bold>
###xml 1528 1529 1496 1497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</italic>
###xml 1717 1721 1685 1689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dhillon1">[43]</xref>
###xml 1722 1726 1690 1694 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Huang1">[66]</xref>
In order to determine whether HML-HMR crosslinking frequencies and colocalization are related to silencing, we measured the level of silencing in the various mutant strains analyzed in this study. Previously, varying silencing defects were observed for the strains described here that display loss of the HML-HMR interactions (sir1Delta, esc2Delta, asf1Delta and cac1Deltahir1Delta) [27],[42],[43]. In most cases silencing defects could be detected using strains that have a reporter gene inserted in one of the HM loci (either URA3 or ADE2). Use of a reporter provides highly sensitive assays to quantify de-repression of HM loci as expression of the reporter gene can be detected even when expressed at very low levels. However, these reporter assays do not quantify the level of mRNA production compared to a fully expressed or repressed state. In order to quantify mRNA levels of the endogenous genes directly in a population of cells we employed RT-PCR to quantify the level of a1 mRNA levels (located at HMR) in MATalpha strains. This allowed us to analyze silencing levels in the same strain in which interactions between HM loci were detected. We observe that deletion of SIR4, SIR3, SIR2, SIR1 or combined deletion of CAC1 and HIR1 as well as a sir2-345 point mutation results in significant de-repression of HMR relative to the Adh1 gene that was used as a normalization control (Figure 8). However, the other two mutants that display loss of the HM-interactions (esc2Delta and asf1Delta) had no detectable levels of a1 expression, and thus had largely normal levels of silencing as determined by RT-PCR. Experiments employing reporter genes also revealed only very minor silencing defects in these strains [43],[66].
###end p 66
###begin title 67
###xml 14 16 14 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Silencing and HM interactions are distinct processes.
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 19 20 19 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 20 21 20 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</italic>
###xml 60 68 60 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT&#945;</italic>
###xml 189 193 185 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADH1</italic>
###xml 276 285 272 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 339 346 331 338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 409 410 401 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 410 411 402 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</italic>
###xml 497 499 489 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
RT-PCR analysis of a1 transcription in wild-type and mutant MATalpha strains analyzed by 3C. Error bar represents standard error of the mean from two independent experiments. Expression of ADH1 was used as an internal control and data was normalized to level of expression in sir3Delta mutants (set at 1). Inset: Crosslinking frequency of HML-HMR interaction is plotted versus the relative mRNA expression of a1 for all mutants analyzed to indicate that no clear correlation between silencing and HM interactions is detected.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 108 110 108 110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 190 192 190 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 207 215 207 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 246 255 246 251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc2&#916;</italic>
###xml 260 269 256 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 271 273 263 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 409 411 401 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
We conclude that all mutants with a significant silencing defect have also lost the interaction between the HM loci. However, we find no clear quantitative correlation between silencing and HM interactions (Figure 8, inset) because in two cases (esc2Delta and asf1Delta) HM interactions are lost, but silencing is mostly unaffected. We conclude that Sir-mediated silencing is not sufficient for clustering of HM loci, and that additional processes in heterochromatin formation are specifically required for associations between heterochromatic loci. These processes require at least Asf1p, Esc2p and possibly Sir1p.
###end p 69
###begin title 70
Discussion
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 70 72 70 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 148 153 148 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 158 163 158 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 426 429 426 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 434 437 434 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 437 441 437 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dekker1">[29]</xref>
###xml 572 575 572 575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 576 579 576 579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 688 691 688 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 692 695 692 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
Here we report specific long-range interaction between the two silent HM loci that is most prominent around their flanking regions encompassing the HML-E and HMR-I silencer elements. This interaction was carefully documented using 3C and 3D live cell imaging technologies in parallel. Previously, we performed 3C on purified nuclei and also found relatively frequent interactions between the ends of chromosome III, including HML and HMR[29]. However, in that analysis the interaction between these loci was significantly lower compared to the data presented here and the HML-HMR interaction was not more frequent than the interaction between the two telomeres. Thus, it appears that the HML-HMR interaction is specifically lost during the nuclear isolation procedure, highlighting the importance of analyzing intact cells.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 24 27 24 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 32 35 32 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 238 240 238 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
The interaction between HML and HMR requires Sir1p, Sir2p, Sir3p, Sir4p and Esc2p as well as nucleosome assembly complexes, known to be involved in establishment and maintenance of heterochromatin at these loci. Our analysis reveals that HM loci can be silenced without clustering and suggests that gene silencing and clustering are distinct properties of heterochromatin. We propose that interaction of heterochromatic domains requires proper chromatin conformation that depends on at least Asf1, Sir1p and Esc2p.
###end p 72
###begin title 73
###xml 39 41 39 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Membrane Association and Clustering of HM Loci Are Independent
###end title 73
###begin p 74
###xml 50 53 50 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 58 61 58 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 298 301 298 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 302 305 302 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 358 367 358 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 426 429 422 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 430 433 426 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
Our live tracking of the sub-nuclear positions of HML and HMR in wild-type cells showed that these loci can colocalize as frequently when these loci are located near the center of the nucleus as when they are near its periphery. Therefore, association with the nuclear envelope is not required for HML-HMR interactions. Further, the results we obtained in a sir3Delta strain show that membrane anchoring is not sufficient for HML-HMR interactions to occur. We conclude that clustering of heterochromatic loci and NE anchoring are two distinct processes that each contribute to nuclear organization.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 71 73 71 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 214 218 214 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 232 237 232 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YKU70</italic>
###xml 279 282 279 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 343 346 343 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 375 394 375 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 521 525 513 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gartenberg1">[46]</xref>
###xml 526 530 518 522 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Taddei1">[48]</xref>
###xml 535 537 527 529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 565 573 557 565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 688 691 680 683 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 696 699 688 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 768 787 760 771 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 945 947 929 931 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 975 985 959 969 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s003">Figure S3D</xref>
Surprisingly, our analyses also reveal that peripheral localization of HM loci is not reduced upon inactivation of the two previously defined pathways for membrane anchoring of heterochromatin. As shown previously [47], deletion of YKU70 increases the peripheral localization of HML in interphase cells, while not affecting the positioning of HMR. In addition, given that in yku70Deltaesc1Delta double mutant cells heterochromatin formation near telomeres is disrupted and Sir4p is found uniformly throughout the nucleus [46],[48] but HM interactions are retained (Figure 5), these data also indicate that sequestration of Sir protein in clusters is not required for interactions between HML and HMR. Consistent with the loss of Sir protein clusters, we found that in yku70Deltaesc1Delta double mutant cells interactions between some telomeres is reduced, as detected by 3C, suggesting that in this mutant telomere clustering is affected, while HM interactions are retained (Figure S3D).
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 41 44 41 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 49 52 49 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 93 103 93 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yku70&#916;</italic>
###xml 105 114 101 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 116 139 108 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">and yku70&#916;esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 406 409 390 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 414 417 398 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 658 660 642 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 713 715 697 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 813 817 797 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gartenberg1">[46]</xref>
###xml 818 822 802 806 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Laroche1">[49]</xref>
###xml 949 951 933 935 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1002 1006 986 990 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Maillet1">[14]</xref>
###xml 1007 1011 991 995 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Maillet2">[51]</xref>
###xml 1070 1072 1054 1056 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1195 1197 1179 1181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1347 1349 1331 1333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1463 1466 1447 1450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1467 1470 1451 1454 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1619 1621 1603 1605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
We observed that the interaction between HML and HMR, as detected by 3C, is more frequent in yku70Delta, esc1Delta, and yku70Deltaesc1Delta mutant cells than in wild-type cells. However, live fluorescence microscopy revealed no increase in their colocalization as compared to wild type cells. This apparent discrepancy may be explained in different ways. First, it is possible that the interaction between HML and HMR is more intimate, and thus more effectively crosslinked, in these mutants, in a manner that is not microscopically distinguishable from wild type. A more intimate association may be the result of an increase in Sir protein occupancy at the HM loci in these mutants. Sir protein occupancy at the HM loci is likely increased in these mutants because telomere silencing and clustering are affected [46],[49]. Loss of Sir proteins from telomeres has been found to increase the available pool of Sir proteins that are accessible to the HM loci, which may enhance their ability to interact [14],[51]. An alternative explanation is that 3C underestimates the HM crosslinking frequency in wild type cells, or overestimates their crosslinking frequency in these mutants. Given that the HM loci interact with each other as well as with telomeres, a loss of telomeric heterochromatin will reduce the number of interaction partners to which HM loci can be cross-linked and ligated during the 3C procedure, resulting in detection of relatively more frequent HML-HMR interactions in these mutants. Although our studies clearly found a strong correlation between 3C crosslinking frequency data and colocalization of HM loci, future experiments are needed to further quantify the relationship between 3C data and data obtained by fluorescence microscopy.
###end p 76
###begin title 77
###xml 0 2 0 2 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
HM Interactions and Silencing Are Related but Mechanistically Distinct Processes
###end title 77
###begin p 78
###xml 234 237 234 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 238 241 238 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 345 347 345 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
The Sir complex and proteins that recruit this complex, as well as histones and nucleosome assembly factors all cooperate to assemble silenced chromatin domains. We find that mutants in each of these protein complexes display loss of HML-HMR interactions. Thus the pathways that mediate heterochromatin formation and the mechanism(s) that drive HM interactions are clearly related and are mediated by overlapping protein complexes. However, several observations indicate that these processes are mechanistically distinct as they differentially depend on specific chromatin factors.
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 20 29 20 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc2&#916;</italic>
###xml 34 43 30 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 97 100 89 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 105 108 97 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 310 313 302 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 346 355 338 343 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 360 369 348 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 378 382 362 366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Huang1">[66]</xref>
###xml 412 415 396 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 475 484 459 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 570 574 550 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ASF1</italic>
###xml 781 788 761 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-HMR</italic>
###xml 898 900 878 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 935 937 915 917 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
First, two mutants (esc2Delta and asf1Delta) that display a complete loss of interaction between HML and HMR display only very minor defects in silencing as detected by RT-PCR. Similar very minor silencing defects have been detected using reporter constructs. Huang et al. used a GFP reporter gene inserted in HMR to detect GFP expression in WT, sir3Delta and asf1Delta strains [66]. They found that in WT cells HMR is silent and only 0.3% of cells expressed GFP, whereas in sir3Delta cells the locus was mostly derepressed with 99% of cells expressing GFP. Deletion of ASF1 resulted in GFP expression in only 0.9% of cells, indicative of effective silencing. Although we cannot formally exclude the possibility that very small defects in silencing are sufficient to cause loss of HML-HMR interactions, we favor the interpretation that heterochromatin formation and silencing is not sufficient for HM interactions, and conversely that HM interactions are not essential for heterochromatin formation.
###end p 79
###begin p 80
###xml 90 94 90 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
###xml 139 141 139 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 260 264 260 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIR1</italic>
###xml 266 270 266 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAC1</italic>
###xml 274 278 274 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ASF1</italic>
###xml 317 321 317 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Enomoto1">[26]</xref>
###xml 322 326 322 326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
###xml 327 331 327 331 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Huang1">[66]</xref>
###xml 332 336 332 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Tyler2">[67]</xref>
###xml 359 363 359 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ASF1</italic>
###xml 383 385 383 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 411 429 411 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cac1&#916;hir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 452 461 444 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 494 497 482 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 498 501 486 489 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 581 585 569 573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
Second, genetic evidence indicates that Hir1p and Asf1p act in the same silencing pathway [27], but they display very different effects on HM interactions, suggesting that for the latter process they act in different pathways. In addition, single deletions of HIR1, CAC1 or ASF1 all result in minor silencing defects [26],[27],[66],[67], but only deletion of ASF1 results in loss of HM interactions. Third, the cac1Deltahir1Delta double mutant and the asf1Delta mutant display the same loss of HML-HMR interactions, but they have quantitatively very different effects on silencing [27], again pointing to differential dependence of silencing and long-range interactions on these chromatin assembly factors.
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 39 43 39 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR1</italic>
###xml 61 63 61 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 130 133 130 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 138 141 138 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 359 363 359 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Pillus1">[42]</xref>
###xml 388 391 388 391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 551 554 527 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 555 558 531 534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 700 709 676 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir4&#916;</italic>
The differential effect of deletion of SIR1 on silencing and HM interactions is particularly interesting. In the absence of Sir1p HML and HMR are partially derepressed. This is due to the occurrence of two distinct populations of chromatin states: in one subset of cells the loci are completely repressed, whereas in the other subset they are fully expressed [42]. Our RT-PCR analysis of HMR expression suggests that approximately60% of loci remain repressed, whereas approximately40% are expressed. However, the 3C analysis showed a complete loss of HML-HMR interactions and the level of colocalization, as determined by live cell 3D imaging was indistinguishable from background levels observed in sir4Delta cells. These results indicate that Sir1p may have a specific role in long-range interactions between heterochromatic loci that is distinct from mediating gene silencing per se.
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 55 58 55 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 63 66 63 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 135 137 135 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 144 147 144 147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 148 151 148 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 360 362 360 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 436 438 436 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Taken together, formation of silent heterochromatin at HML and HMR is essential but not sufficient for long-range interactions between HM loci. HML-HMR interactions require Asf1p, Esc2p and possibly Sir1p in a process that is distinct from silencing. Other proteins, such as other SIR complex components may also play a role in that process, but their role in HM interactions is more difficult to assess, as they are also essential for HM silencing.
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 59 63 59 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ASF1</italic>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Hiraga1">[60]</xref>
###xml 190 194 190 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ASF1</italic>
###xml 230 234 230 234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Sharp1">[27]</xref>
###xml 235 239 235 239 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Tyler2">[67]</xref>
Interestingly, it has recently been shown that deletion of ASF1 shows a telomere-positioning defect, and also affects the sub-nuclear positioning of other chromosomal loci [60]. Deletion of ASF1 does not affect telomere silencing [27],[67], suggesting that silencing of telomeres is not sufficient for their positioning. Combined with our data, these results point to a specific Asf1p - dependent process that is required for heterochromatic positioning in the nucleus in general.
###end p 83
###begin title 84
Potential Role of Silencer Elements in Long-Range Interactions
###end title 84
###begin p 85
###xml 35 40 35 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 45 50 45 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 107 109 107 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 228 231 228 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 231 235 231 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Donze1">[68]</xref>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 280 285 280 285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 290 295 290 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 499 503 499 503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Triolo1">[69]</xref>
###xml 504 508 504 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gardner1">[70]</xref>
###xml 570 574 570 574 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Suter1">[71]</xref>
###xml 642 646 642 646 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Franco1">[72]</xref>
###xml 705 710 705 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 791 793 791 793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 820 825 820 825 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 898 901 898 901 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
Restriction fragments encompassing HML-E and HMR-I interact most frequently compared to other parts of the HM loci. These restriction fragments do not contain the boundary elements that have been identified up and downstream of HMR[68], suggesting the HM interaction involves the HML-E and HMR-I silencer elements specifically. Interestingly, one protein that we identified as critical for long-range interactions, Sir1p, associates with replication related complexes bound to the silencer elements [69],[70], and another (Asf1p) displays genetic interactions with ORC2 [71] and physically associates with other replication factors such RF-C [72]. Unfortunately, we have not been able to precisely delete HMR-I so we have not been able to directly test the role of this element in mediating HM interactions. Deletion of HML-E would not address this issue as it would also result in derepression of HML.
###end p 85
###begin p 86
###xml 163 166 163 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 168 173 168 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 178 183 178 183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Valenzuela1">[28]</xref>
###xml 275 278 275 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 320 323 320 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sau</italic>
###xml 349 352 349 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 368 371 368 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 403 406 403 406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 407 410 407 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 452 457 452 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 458 463 458 463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-I</italic>
###xml 493 496 493 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
Our results are different from those recently described by Kamakaka and co-workers, who reported Sir3p-dependent looping interactions between the two silencers of HMR, HMR-E and HMR-I[28]. One explanation for this difference could be the fact that they used strains in which HMR was slightly modified to introduce extra Sau3A restriction sites, and HML and the active MAT locus were deleted, precluding HMR-HML interactions. However, we did not detect HML-E-HML-I interactions when we deleted HMR in our strain background (not shown). An alternative explanation is that different strain backgrounds were used.
###end p 86
###begin title 87
Clustering of Heterochromatic Loci and Nuclear Compartmentalization
###end title 87
###begin p 88
###xml 4 7 4 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 8 11 8 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
The HML-HMR association is not essential for silencing, suggesting that the role of this interaction in silencing is either highly redundant with other pathways that contribute to heterochromatin formation or that it is involved in other processes, such as mating type switching or contributing to higher order nuclear organization in general.
###end p 88
###begin p 89
###xml 39 41 39 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 168 171 168 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 171 172 171 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 171 172 171 172 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 176 184 176 180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT&#945;</italic>
###xml 379 383 375 379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Wu1">[73]</xref>
###xml 384 388 380 384 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bressan1">[74]</xref>
###xml 620 623 616 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 628 635 624 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR in </italic>
###xml 635 636 631 632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 635 636 631 632 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 655 671 647 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s002">Figure S2C and D</xref>
###xml 758 761 750 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 766 769 758 761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 805 809 797 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 918 927 910 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1&#916;</italic>
###xml 932 941 920 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">esc2&#916;</italic>
###xml 1009 1025 993 1005 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HO/&#8221; asf1&#916;/&#8221;</italic>
###xml 1029 1045 1009 1021 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HO/&#8221; esc2&#916;/&#8221;</italic>
###xml 1256 1258 1232 1234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Various lines of evidence suggest that HM-interactions are not involved in mating type switching. First, we did not detect any differences in the interaction in either MATa or MATalpha cells, despite well-characterized mating-type-dependent differences between the left and right arm of chromosome III with regards to mobility and accessibility for recombination complexes [e.g. [73],[74]]. Second, we also analyzed mutants in which the recombination enhancer (RE), an element known to mediate donor preference in mating type switching, was deleted and observed only a minor increase in crosslinking frequencies between HML and HMR in a- or alpha- cells (Figure S2C and D). In addition, previous studies also revealed no difference in nuclear positioning of HML and HMR in mutants when the RE was deleted [47] (and data not shown). Lastly, we tested directly whether any mating type switching defect was observable in asf1Delta and esc2Delta mutants. We analyzed the mating proficiency of meiotic products of HO/" asf1Delta/" or HO/" esc2Delta/" strains and found that spore colonies did not mate with a tester strain, indicating that spores efficiently self-diploidized and thus were fully capable of switching (data not shown). Thus, it appears that the HM-interaction does not play a critical role in mating type switching.
###end p 89
###begin p 90
###xml 20 23 20 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 24 27 24 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 186 194 186 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 245 247 245 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 356 358 356 358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1320 1324 1320 1324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Taddei2">[75]</xref>
We propose that the HML-HMR interaction plays primarily a structural role by contributing to clustering of heterochromatin and formation of heterochromatic sub-nuclear compartments (see Figure 9 for model). In the absence of silencing proteins, HM-loci are not silenced and do not interact. Upon expression of silencing proteins, they are recruited to the HM-silencers resulting in heterochromatin formation and silencing. This step requires the presence of SIR proteins and the CAF-1/HIR1 complex for proper nucleosome assembly. Once silenced, these loci then engage in long-range interactions, which are dependent upon the presence of Asf1p, Esc2p, and Sir1p. Once heterochromatic clusters are formed, the nuclear distribution of silencer proteins becomes highly non-homogeneous with high local concentrations in the silent compartments and depletion in the rest of the nucleus. Nuclear compartmentalization could be advantageous because only loci located within the silent compartments will have access to abundant silencer proteins while the rest of the genome is precluded from inadvertently gaining access to heterochromatin proteins. Consistent with this model, a recent study showed that loss of heterochromatic clustering resulted in inappropriate Sir-mediated ectopic repression of genes throughout the genome [75].
###end p 90
###begin title 91
Clustering of silent chromatin.
###end title 91
###begin p 92
###xml 67 69 67 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 76 79 76 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 98 101 98 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 272 274 272 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 961 963 961 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
In the absence of silencing proteins, depicted as colored circles, HM-loci (HML- black rectangle; HMR- gray rectangle) are not silenced and they do not form clusters. Upon expression, silencing proteins are available throughout the nucleus and can become recruited to the HM silencers, independent of their sub-nuclear position. Heterochromatin is formed and silencing is established. Once these loci are silenced, they obtain the ability to form clusters that can also contain telomeres. Silent clusters create sub-nuclear compartments in which there is a high local concentration of silencing proteins available for recruitment to loci located within the cluster only. Membrane association of silenced loci will anchor clusters or unclustered loci to the nuclear periphery. Loci located outside heterochromatin compartments have no access to silencing proteins and are not silenced. In this model clustering, membrane anchoring as well a genomic proximity of HM loci to telomeres will all contribute to formation of sub-nuclear compartments that are enriched in silencing complexes, which will facilitate heterochromatin formation at resident loci.
###end p 92
###begin title 93

###end title 93

###begin p 95

###xml 163 169 163 169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RTT109</italic>
###xml 271 275 271 275 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Wach1">[76]</xref>
###xml 293 301 293 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2-345</italic>
###xml 326 330 326 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Imai1">[23]</xref>

###xml 414 423 414 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir2&#916;</italic>
###xml 497 518 493 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s006">Supplementary Table 2</xref>
###xml 739 747 729 737 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s006">Table S2</xref>
###xml 840 844 830 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky3">[77]</xref>
###xml 976 979 966 969 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 999 1002 989 992 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1025 1028 1015 1018 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 1167 1171 1157 1161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky3">[77]</xref>
###xml 1172 1176 1162 1166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dubrana1">[79]</xref>
###xml 1218 1221 1208 1211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tet</italic>
###xml 1221 1223 1211 1213 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">op</sup>
###xml 1228 1231 1218 1221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lac</italic>
###xml 1231 1233 1221 1223 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">op</sup>
###xml 1261 1263 1251 1253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1295 1299 1285 1289 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky1">[30]</xref>
###xml 630 635 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
HMR, SIR1, SIR2, SIR3, SIR4, CAC1, ASF1, ESC2, KU70, KU80, ESC1, HIR1, the recombination enhancer (RE) located on chromosome III (SGD coordinates 29017-29799) and RTT109 were replaced with antibiotic resistance markers using a standard PCR based gene disruption strategy [76]. To generate the sir2-345 mutant, plasmid pRS 345 [23], which is linked to LEU2 was cut with Hpa1 and integrated into chromosome III in a sir2Delta background. All strains used for 3C were maintained in a SK1 background (Supplementary Table 2). Cells were freshly streaked on YPD medium containing 2% glucose before 3C analysis. For microscopy analyses, yeast were grown at 30degreesC in rich glucose media (YPD) unless otherwise indicated. Strains are listed in Table S2. Plasmids used to integrate the tet or lac operator arrays and repressors were as described [77]. The following PCR-amplified genomic fragments (SGD coordinates) were used for insertion near the respective loci: 15160-15773 for HML, 294892-295241 for HMR and 197194-196910 for MAT on Chr3. LacI-GFP or lacI-CFP, and tetR-GFP or tetR-YFP, and where indicated GFP-Nup49 or CFP-Nup49 fusions, were introduced as described [77]-[79]. Note that the wild type strain with the tetop and lacop operator inserted near the HM loci has been described before [30].
###end p 95
###begin title 96
Image Acquisition and Manipulation
###end title 96
###begin p 97
###xml 124 130 124 130 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600 nm</sub>
###xml 156 157 144 145 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
For live and intact cell imaging, cultures carrying two color tagged integration sites were grown exponentially in YPD to OD600 nm< = 0.4 (approximately1x107 cells/ml), and rinsed in complete synthetic medium before imaging. Microscopy was performed at 25degreesC. Cells were spread on synthetic complete 3% agarose patches for acquisition.
###end p 97
###begin p 98
###xml 751 755 747 751 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky2">[47]</xref>
###xml 756 760 752 756 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Hediger2">[50]</xref>
###xml 960 964 956 960 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Schober1">[80]</xref>
3D images were captured on a Metamorph driven Olympus IX81 wide-field microscope equipped with a Coolsnap HQ camera and a Polychrome V (Till Photonics). Stacks of 21 images were acquired with a step size of 0.2 microm either at 490 nm for 200 ms for GFP or alternating the wavelength between 435 nm (CFP) and 512 nm (YFP) at every image plane, and exposures of 400 ms per wavelength. A 100x/1.4 Oil Plan-Apochromat objective (Olympus) was used. Position of GFP tagged loci relative to the nuclear rim identified by the Nup49-GFP signal were determined as a percentage of fluorescent spots in one of three concentric nuclear zones of equal surface in the plane bearing the brightest GFP-lacI or tetR-GFP focus using the Pointpicker plug-in for Image J [47],[50]. Only the 10 core focal planes were scored. For 3D distance determination, CFP and YFP images were automatically analyzed using SpotDistance implemented as a plug-in for ImageJ, freely available at: [80]. The measured distances were loaded into R software () and the measured distance distributions translated into a box plot. Outliers are defined as 1.5 times the Inter Quartile Range (IQR) and are represented as open circles. Different distance distributions (determined as non-normal using a Kolmogorov-Smirnov test) were scored for significant difference in R using the Wilcox test.
###end p 98
###begin p 99
###xml 23 32 23 32 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000478-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 314 318 314 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Bystricky1">[30]</xref>
2D time-lapse imaging (Figure 6B) was performed on a Zeiss LSM510 confocal microscope using a 100x Plan-Apochromat objective (NA = 1.4) partly at the RIO Imaging facility in Toulouse, France, and partly in Susan Gasser's laboratory at the University of Geneva, Switzerland. Live imaging was performed as described [30]. Nine independent 2D time-lapse series of 50 to 150 confocal images were acquired at 1.5 s intervals of G1-phase nuclei, following the tagged foci by adjusting the focal plane. 2D distances were measured manually using Metamorph.
###end p 99
###begin title 100
3C Analysis
###end title 100
###begin p 101
###xml 86 92 86 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 92 95 92 95 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Miele1">[4]</xref>
###xml 96 100 96 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dekker1">[29]</xref>
###xml 101 105 101 105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Miele2">[32]</xref>
###xml 154 157 154 157 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 255 256 255 256 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 269 270 269 270 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1363 1373 1351 1361 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s003">Figure S3C</xref>
3C was performed as described by Dekker et al., with modifications described in Miele et al.[4],[29],[32]. Cells were freshly grown in YPD medium to an OD600 of 1.0. Cells were then resuspended in buffer containing 0.4 M sorbitol, 0.4 M KCl, 40 mM Na(H)PO4, 0.5 mM MgCl2, and 0.1 mg/mL of zymolyase 100-T and incubated at 30degreesC for 40 minutes. Efficiency of the digestion of cell wall was tested by observation of hypotonic lysis within 1-2 minutes. Spheroplasts were washed three times in a buffer containing 0.1 M MES, 1.2 M sorbitol, 1 mM EDTA, and 0.5 mM MgCl2 and then resuspended in the same buffer. Formaldehyde was added to a final concentration of 1% and crosslinking was allowed to proceed for ten minutes at room temperature. The reaction was quenched by addition of glycine to a final concentration of 125 mM and incubation for 5 minutes at room temperature. Cells were washed three times and resuspended in the restriction enzyme buffer. Chromatin was solubilized by the addition of 0.1% final concentration of SDS and incubation for 10 minutes at 65degreesC. Trition X-100 was added to a final concentration of 1%. A restriction enzyme was added and samples were incubated overnight at the appropriate incubation temperature. The digestion efficiency was determined to be 80% and this percentage did not vary between restriction cut sites (see Figure S3C). The restriction enzyme was inactivated by addition of SDS to a final concentration of 1.6% followed by incubation at 65degreesC for 20 minutes. Chromatin was diluted for ligation to promote intramolecular ligation over intermolecular ligation. Triton X-100 was added to 1% and DNA was ligated for 2 hours at 16degreesC with T4 DNA ligase. The cross-links are reversed overnight by incubation at 65degreesC in the presence of 5 microgram/ml of proteinase K. After overnight incubation an additional 5 microgram/ml of proteinase K was added and incubated for an additional 2 hours at 42degreesC. DNA was purified by a series of phenol-chloroform extractions followed by ethanol precipitation. The resulting template was then treated with RNAse A.
###end p 101
###begin p 102
###xml 240 245 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
In addition to the above 3C template a randomized control template was also generated which is used to determine PCR amplification efficiency of specific 3C ligation products. This template was created by digesting purified non-crosslinked yeast genomic DNA which is then followed by a random intermolecular ligation. The resulting template was purified by a series of phenol-chloroform extractions and ethanol precipitations. The resulting template was also treated with RNAse A.
###end p 102
###begin p 103
###xml 183 199 183 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s001">Figure S1A and B</xref>
###xml 310 311 306 307 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 804 808 760 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Tolhuis1">[39]</xref>
###xml 809 813 765 769 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Splinter2">[81]</xref>
###xml 814 818 770 774 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Hagge1">[82]</xref>
###xml 1527 1535 1483 1491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s007">Table S3</xref>
Once both the 3C templates and control templates are generated a PCR titration is performed to determine the amount of template to be used in the subsequent PCR reactions as shown in Figure S1A and B. PCR is performed in a 50 microl reaction in a buffer containing 10 mM Tris-Cl pH 8.4, 50 mM KCl, 2.25 mM MgCl2, 0.5 mM dNTPs and 0.4 microM of each primer. The following PCR program gives quantitative results: 32 times: 1 minute at 95degreesC, 45 seconds at 60degreesC, 2 minutes at 72degreesC. This is followed by 1 minute at 95degreesC, 45 seconds at 60degreesC, and 8 minutes at 72degreesC. PCR products are quantified semi-quantitatively on 1.5% agarose gels in the presence of ethidium bromide. Previous work displays that semi-quantitative PCR and quantitative real-time PCR yield similar results [39],[81],[82]. Multiple primer combinations are used that detect highly abundant 3C ligation products as well as infrequently formed products to be sure that the amount of template used in each reaction is within the linear range. The subsequent PCR reactions are done in triplicate for both the control and 3C template. The crosslinking frequency is then determined by calculating the ratio between the amount of PCR product obtained with the 3C template and the control template. The three resulting crosslinking frequencies are then averaged together and one value is obtained. This is the value that is plotted in interaction graphs. The standard deviation of the mean is determined and is used as the error bars (see Table S3 for examples of crosslinking frequency determination).
###end p 103
###begin p 104
###xml 145 150 145 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-I</italic>
###xml 152 157 152 157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 159 164 159 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 166 171 166 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-I</italic>
###xml 290 298 290 298 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s005">Table S1</xref>
###xml 317 327 317 327 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s001">Figure S1C</xref>
###xml 343 348 343 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EcoRI</italic>
Restriction enzymes were chosen to create an equal distribution of restriction fragment cut sites and also to allow for important elements (i.e. HMR-I, HMR-E, HML-E, HML-I, etc) to be on different restriction fragments. Primers were then designed for restriction fragments of interest (see Table S1 for sequences and Figure S1C for diagram of EcoRI primers). Primers were designed unidirectionally unless a unique primer could not be designed on that particular end of the fragment. They were designed to be approximately 28 base pairs long with 50% GC content. Once designed, the primers were tested on a control template and those primers that give aberrant products, multiple products, and abundant primer dimers were re-designed.
###end p 104
###begin p 105
###xml 186 195 186 195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s004">Figure S4</xref>
3C analyses for wild type and each mutant described above were performed in at least two, and in most cases three independent experiments, with each data point quantified in triplicate. Figure S4 displays some examples of biological repeats of 3C analyses that illustrate the highly reproducible nature of 3C interaction profiles in WT and several mutant strains.
###end p 105
###begin p 106
###xml 57 58 57 58 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</bold>
###xml 141 145 141 145 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gheldof1">[33]</xref>
###xml 146 150 146 150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dekker2">[34]</xref>
###xml 196 204 192 196 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hmr&#916;</italic>
###xml 228 246 220 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ku70&#916;esc1&#916;</italic>
###xml 252 270 236 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cac1&#916;hir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 651 656 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
All 3C data are normalized to the wild type (mating type a) dataset so that all interactions can be quantitatively compared, as described in [33],[34]. Datasets for wild-type (mating type alpha), hmrDelta fine mapping analyses, ku70Deltaesc1Delta, and cac1Deltahir1Delta mutants strains were normalized by calculating the average log ratio of crosslinking frequencies between the anchor fragment and neighboring fragments measured within each of the different strains as compared to wild type and setting this ratio at zero. For data normalization with all other mutants, 8 crosslinking frequencies were determined between pairs of loci located along yeast chromosome VI. Data normalization was performed by calculating the average log ratio of the set of 8 crosslinking frequencies measured in each mutant as compared to wild type and adjusting the mutant data sets so that this ratio becomes zero.
###end p 106
###begin title 107
Digestion Efficiency Determination
###end title 107
###begin p 108
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 67 70 67 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 96 99 96 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 267 270 267 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 702 705 702 705 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 782 786 782 786 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Gheldof1">[33]</xref>
###xml 787 791 787 791 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dekker2">[34]</xref>
###xml 875 878 875 878 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 907 917 907 917 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000478.s003">Figure S3C</xref>
###xml 1006 1010 1006 1010 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Dekker2">[34]</xref>
###xml 1164 1167 1164 1167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1172 1175 1172 1175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 163 168 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
EcoRI cutting efficiency was determined for a fragment upstream of HML, the fragment containing HML, and a fragment at the left telomere of chromosome III. Intact yeast cells were treated with 1% formaldehyde. Chromatin was solubilized and one part was digested with EcoRI while the other part was not. Cross-links were reversed and the DNA was purified. Semi-quantitative PCR was done across restriction fragments on both samples and the ratio of PCR products was calculated to determine the percentage of loci that were not digested upon formaldehyde cross-linking. The data was normalized for the amount of DNA used in each reaction using a pair of primers that amplify a region contained within an EcoRI fragment. Digestion efficiency was comparable to that reported previously [33],[34]. The level of digestion was around 75-80%, and was not significantly different for HML as compared to other sites (Figure S3C). Given that the digestion efficiency is linearly related to the level of cross-linking [34], this result also implies that the level of cross-linking is similar at these locations. We conclude that the peak in crosslinking frequency observed at HML and HMR is not due to differences in digestion or cross-linking.
###end p 108
###begin title 109
RT-PCR
###end title 109
###begin p 110
###xml 330 331 330 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 330 331 330 331 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 331 332 331 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</italic>
###xml 367 373 367 373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 373 377 373 377 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000478-Smeal1">[83]</xref>
###xml 400 404 400 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADH1</italic>
Total RNA was isolated by using the RNeasy Mini Kit (Qiagen, Valencia, CA). cDNA was synthesized using the SuperScript First-Strand Synthesis for RT-PCR protocol including DNase I treatment as described (Invitrogen.com). The cDNA was synthesized using oligodT12-18 (Invitrogen) and then was amplified by PCR. Primer sequences for a1 expression are described by Smeal et al.[83]. Primer sequences for ADH1, which was used as the internal control, are available upon request.
###end p 110

###end title 111

###xml 205 208 205 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 213 216 213 216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>

###xml 226 234 222 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT&#945;</italic>
###xml 289 292 281 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>

###xml 420 436 412 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RE&#916; MAT&#945;</italic>
###xml 497 500 481 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 523 526 507 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 624 635 608 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RE&#916; MAT</italic>
###xml 635 636 615 616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 635 636 615 616 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 690 693 670 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 716 719 696 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 817 820 797 800 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 820 821 800 801 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 820 821 800 801 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 876 879 856 859 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 1021 1024 1001 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAT</italic>
###xml 1024 1025 1004 1005 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 1024 1025 1004 1005 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>a</italic></bold>
###xml 1080 1083 1060 1063 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
